<HEAD>
<TITLE>Certification</TITLE>
<META NAME="author" CONTENT="Steven Taylor">
<META NAME="date" CONTENT="08/16/2016">
</HEAD>
<BODY style="margin-top:0;font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt; 
color:#000000">
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial-BoldMT,Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=center><B>CERTIFICATION OF INTERIM FILINGS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial-BoldMT,Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=center><B>VENTURE ISSUER BASIC CERTIFICATE</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify>I,
J. Paul Sorbara<FONT style="font-family:Arial"><B><I>, Chief Executive Officer 
of Golden Goliath Resources Ltd., </I></B></FONT>certify the following:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify>1.
<FONT style="font-family:Arial"><B><I>Review: </I></B></FONT>I have reviewed the
interim financial report and interim MD&amp;A (together the interim filings) of 
<FONT style="font-family:Arial-BoldMT,Arial"><B>Golden Goliath Resources Ltd. 
</B></FONT>(the issuer) for the interim period ended <FONT style="font-
family:Arial"><B><I>May 31, 2016.</I></B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify>2.
<FONT style="font-family:Arial"><B><I>No misrepresentations: 
</I></B></FONT>Based on my knowledge, having exercised reasonable diligence, the
interim filings do not contain any untrue statement of a material fact or omit 
to state a material fact required to be stated or that is necessary to make a 
statement not misleading in light of the circumstances under which it was made, 
with respect to the period covered by the interim filings.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify>3.
<FONT style="font-family:Arial"><B><I>Fair presentation: </I></B></FONT>Based on
my knowledge having exercised reasonable diligence, the interim financial report
together with the other financial information included in the interim filings 
fairly present in all material respects the financial condition, financial 
performance and cash flows of the issuer, as for the date of and for the periods
presented in the interim filings.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial; font-size:9pt">Date: <FONT 
style="font-family:Arial"><B><I>July 27, 2016</I></B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt"><I>&#148;J. Paul 
Sorbara&#148;</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial; font-
size:9pt">______________________</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial-BoldMT,Arial; font-size:9pt"><B>Chief
Executive Officer</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial-BoldMT,Arial" align=center><B>NOTE TO 
READER</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial" align=justify>In contrast to 
the certificate required for non-venture issuers under National Instrument 52-
109 Certification of Disclosure in Issuers' Annual and Interim Filings (NI 52-
109), this Venture Issuer Basic Certificate does not include representations 
relating to the establishment and maintenance of disclosure controls and 
procedures (DC&amp;P) and internal control over financial reporting (ICFR), as 
defined in NI 52-109. In particular, the certifying officers filing this 
certificate are not making any representations relating to the establishment and
maintenance of:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial" align=justify>i) controls and 
other procedures designed to provide reasonable assurance that information 
required to be disclosed by the issuer in its annual filings, interim filings or
other reports filed or submitted under securities legislation is recorded, 
processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified in 
securities legislation; and</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial" align=justify>ii) a process to 
provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting 
and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance 
with the issuer's GAAP.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial" align=justify>The issuer's 
certifying officers are responsible for ensuring that processes are in place to 
provide them with sufficient knowledge to support the representations they are 
making in this certificate.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:ArialMT,Arial" align=justify>Investors should 
be aware that inherent limitations on the ability of certifying officers of a 
venture issuer to design and implement on a cost effective basis DC&amp;P and 
ICFR as defined in NI 52-109 may result in additional risks to the quality, 
reliability, transparency and timeliness of interim and annual filings and other
reports provided under securities legislation</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

in Canadian Dollars)</P>

align=center><B>GOLDEN GOLIATH RESOURCES LTD.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt"

<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center><B>FOR THE NINE MONTHS ENDED MAY 31, 2016 AND 2015</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center>(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center>(unaudited)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>1.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>NATURE OF 
OPERATIONS AND GOING CONCERN</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman;
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Golden Goliath Resources Ltd. (the 
&#147;Company&#148;) was incorporated on June 12, 1996 under the Business 
Corporations Act of British Columbia, Canada. &nbsp;The Company is a public 
company listed on the TSX Venture Exchange (the &#147;TSX.V&#148;), trading 
under the symbol &#147;GNG&#148;. The address of the Company&#146;s corporate 
office and principal place of business is Suite 711, 675 West Hastings Street, 
Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s principal business
activity is the acquisition and exploration of resource properties.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The Company is in the exploration stage and is in 
the process of evaluating its Mexican resource properties and has not yet 
determined whether these properties contain reserves that are economically 
recoverable. &nbsp;The recoverability of amounts shown for exploration and 
evaluation assets are dependent upon the discovery of economically recoverable 
reserves, confirmation of the Company&#146;s interest in the underlying mineral 
claims, the ability of the Company to obtain necessary financing to complete the
development of the properties and upon future profitable production or proceeds 
from the disposition thereof. &nbsp;Managements&#146; plan in this regard is to 
secure additional funds through future equity financings, which either may not 
be available or may not be available on reasonable terms.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The consolidated financial statements have been 
prepared on the basis of accounting principles applicable to a going concern. 
This assumes the Company will operate for the foreseeable future and will be 
able to realize its assets and discharge its liabilities in the normal course of
operations. Accordingly, they do not give effect to adjustments that would be 
necessary should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern and 
therefore be required to realize its assets and liquidate its liabilities, 
contingent obligations and commitments other than in the normal course of 
business and at amounts different from those in the financial statements. The 
Company has incurred operating losses since inception, has no source of 
operating cash flow, minimal income from short-term investments, and there can 
be no assurances that sufficient funding, including adequate financing, will be 
available to complete the exploration of its mineral properties and to cover 
general and administrative expenses necessary for the maintenance of a public 
company. The ability of the Company to arrange additional financing in the 
future depends in part, on the prevailing capital market conditions and mineral 
property exploration success. These factors cast substantial doubt on the 
Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. Accordingly, the 
financial statements do not give effect to adjustments that would be necessary 
should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern and therefore be 
required to realize its assets and liquidate its liabilities, contingent 
obligations and commitments other than in the normal course of business and at 
amounts different from those in the financial statements. &nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>2.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>BASIS OF 
PRESENTATION</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:24px; width:48px; 
font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>a)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Statement of 
Compliance </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>These consolidated financial statements have been 
prepared in accordance with International Financial Reporting Standards 
(&#147;IFRS&#148;) as issued by the International Accounting Standards Board
(&#147;IASB&#148;) which the Company has adopted in its annual consolidated 
financial statements as at and for the year ended August 31, 2015. The 
significant accounting policies presented in this note have been consistently 
applied in each of the years presented.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:24px; width:48.933px; 
font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>b)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48.933px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Basis of 
Preparation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:47.267px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>These consolidated financial statements have been 
prepared on a historical cost basis except for financial instruments that have 
been measured at fair value. These consolidated financial statements have also 
been prepared using the accrual basis of accounting, except for cash flow 
information. &nbsp;In the opinion of management, all adjustments (including 
normal recurring accruals), considered necessary for a fair presentation have 
been included.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48.933px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Foreign Currencies
</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The Company&#146;s reporting currency and 
functional currency is the Canadian dollar. &nbsp;Transactions in United States 
(&#147;US&#148;) and Mexican (&#147;MXN&#148;) foreign currencies have been 
translated into Canadian dollars as follows:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:48px; width:72px; 
font-family:Symbol; font-size:9pt; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Monetary items at the rate prevailing at the 
statement of financial position date;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:48px; width:72px; 
font-family:Symbol; font-size:9pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Non-monetary items at the historical exchange 
rate;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:48px; width:72px; 
font-family:Symbol; font-size:9pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Revenues and expenses at the average rate in effect
during the applicable accounting period; and</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:48px; width:72px; 
font-family:Symbol; font-size:9pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Gains or losses arising on foreign currency 
translation are included in the statements of operations and comprehensive 
loss.</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:24px; width:48.933px; 
font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>d)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48.933px; padding-right:-30px; text-indent:-
2px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Significant Accounting 
Judgments and Estimates</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The preparation of financial statements in conformity with IFRS 
requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported 
amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosures of contingent assets and 
liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of 
revenues and expenses during the reporting period. The preparation of financial 
statements also requires management to exercise judgment in the process of 
applying the accounting policies.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>On an on-going basis, management evaluates its judgments and 
estimates in relation to assets, liabilities and expenses. &nbsp;Management uses
historical experience and various other factors it believes to be reasonable 
under the given circumstances, as the basis for its judgments and estimates. 
&nbsp;Revisions to accounting estimates are recognized prospectively from the 
period in which the estimates are revised. &nbsp;Actual outcomes may differ from
those estimates under different assumptions and conditions.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt"
align=justify><U>Critical Accounting Estimates</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The following are the key estimate and assumption uncertainties 
that have a significant risk of resulting in a material adjustment within the 
next financial year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><I>Impairment</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>Assets, especially exploration and evaluation assets are reviewed 
for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that their 
carrying amounts exceed their recoverable amounts. &nbsp;The assessment of the 
carrying amount often requires estimates and assumptions such as discount rates,
exchange rates, commodity prices, future capital requirements and future 
operating performance.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><I>Share-based payment transactions</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company measures the cost of equity-settled transactions with 
employees by reference to the fair value of the equity instruments at the date 
at which they are granted. &nbsp;Estimating fair value for share-based payment 
transactions requires determining the most appropriate valuation model, which is
dependent on the terms and conditions of the grant of shares. &nbsp;This 
estimate also requires determining the most appropriate inputs to the valuation 
model including the expected life of a share option, volatility and dividend 
yield and making assumptions about them. &nbsp;The assumptions and model used 
for estimating fair value for share-based payment transactions are disclosed in 
Note 7.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-

PRESENTATION </B>(Continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:24px; width:48px; 
font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>d)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:-30px; text-indent:-2px; 
font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Significant 
Accounting Judgments and Estimates</B> (Continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><U>Critical Judgments Used in Applying Accounting 
Policies</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Title to mineral property interests</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Although the Company has taken steps to verify 
title to mineral properties in which it has an interest, these procedures do not
guarantee the Company&#146;s title. &nbsp;Such properties may be subject to 
prior agreements or transfers and title may be affected by undetected 
defects.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Exploration and evaluation expenditures</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The application of the Company&#146;s accounting 
policy for exploration and evaluation expenditures requires judgment in 
determining whether it is likely that future economic benefits will flow to the 
Company, which may be based on assumptions about future events or circumstances.
Estimates and assumptions made may change if new information becomes available. 
If, after the expenditure is capitalized, information becomes available 
suggesting that the recovery of the expenditure is unlikely, the amount 
capitalized is written off in the statement of operations in the period the new 
information becomes available.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Income taxes</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Significant judgment is required in determining the
provision for income taxes. &nbsp;There are many transactions and calculations 
undertaken during the ordinary course of business for which the ultimate tax 
determination is uncertain. &nbsp;The Company recognizes liabilities and 
contingencies for anticipated tax audit issues based on the Company&#146;s 
current understanding of the tax law. &nbsp;For matters where it is probable 
that an adjustment will be made, the Company records its best estimate of the 
tax liability including the related interest and penalties in the current tax
provision. Management believes they have adequately provided for the probable 
outcome of these matters; however, the final outcome may result in a materially 
different outcome than the amount included in the tax liabilities.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>In addition, the Company recognizes deferred tax 
assets relating to tax losses carried forward to the extent there are sufficient
taxable temporary differences (deferred tax liabilities) relating to the same 
taxation authority and the same taxable entity against which the unused tax 
losses can be utilized. &nbsp;However, utilization of the tax losses also 
depends on the ability of the taxable entity to satisfy certain tests at the 
time the losses are recouped. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Decommissioning liabilities</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Judgment is required to determine if there are 
legal or constructive obligations to incur restoration, rehabilitation and 
environmental costs when there is an environmental disturbance caused by 
exploration, development or ongoing productions of an exploration and evaluation
asset. When it is determined that an obligation exists, a provision is 
recognized. The provision for decommissioning liabilities depends on estimates 
of current risk-free interest rates, future restoration and reclamation 
expenditures and the timing of those expenditures. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>3.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>MARKETABLE 
SECURITIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Marketable securities consist of nil (August 31, 
2015 &#150; 425,000) common shares of Comstock Metals Ltd. with a fair value of 
$Nil (August 31, 2015 - $10,625).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Marketable securities are measured at fair value 
with changes in fair value recorded in other comprehensive income (loss) until 
the investment is derecognized or impaired, at which time the gain (loss) would 
be recorded in net income.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>EXPLORATION AND 
EVALUATION ASSETS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>Detailed exploration and evaluation expenditures incurred in 
respect to the Company&#146;s mineral property interests owned, leased or held 
under option are disclosed in Note 13. &nbsp;Property payments made on the 
Company&#146;s mineral property interests are included in the property 
descriptions below. &nbsp;Acquisition costs paid through May 31, 2016 and August
31, 2015 are as follows:</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The Company has an extensive property portfolio of 
mining concessions, acquired mainly through staking, in the Uruachic District of
Mexico covering approximately 10,000 hectares. The Company has various net 
smelter returns on specific claims forming a part of the Company&#146;s 
properties. The net smelter returns range from 1% to 3%, which have buyouts 
ranging from US$250,000 to US$2,000,000.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>In May 2007 and amended April 2011, the Company 
optioned to Comstock Metals Ltd. (&#147;Comstock&#148;) the right to earn up to 
a 75% and 60% interest respectively in the Corona and El Chamizal properties in 
exchange for Comstock spending $500,000 and $200,000 on the respective 
properties before February 8, 2014, and issuing 300,000 (300,000 common shares 
received) and 150,000 (25,000 common shares received) common shares respectively
to the Company over a period of two years. In order to keep the option in good 
standing, Comstock paid $50,000 and issued an additional 200,000 common shares
to the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The Company has received notice from Comstock that 
it has spent in excess of $1,000,000 at Corona and effective April 9, 2013, the 
Company and Comstock entered into a joint venture agreement to further explore 
the property whereby Comstock will act as the operator. The Company is 
responsible for 40% of all exploration costs going forward. &nbsp;The Company 
has been advised that Comstock does not wish to proceed with the joint venture, 
as such the Company is responsible for 100% of the Corona costs.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center><B>FOR THE NINE MONTHS ENDED MAY 31, 2016 AND 2015</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center>(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center>(unaudited)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>5.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>EXPLORATION AND 
EVALUATION ASSETS</B> (Continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>During the year ended August 31, 2015, $81,214 
(2014 - $2,883,086) in deferred expenditures related to certain mineral claims 
were written down. These write-downs were mainly related to the Company&#146;s 
San Timoteo/Bufalo (2014 &#150; San Timoteo/Oro Leon) Property. &nbsp;A number
of other smaller claims were written off which the Company will continue to hold
but which are not viewed as priorities. Management does not currently intend to 
conduct any exploration activities on these non core claims in the next 
year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>On November 5, 2015, the Company signed a 
definitive agreement with Fresnillo PLC (&#147;Fresnillo&#148;) granting 
Fresnillo an option over certain of the Company&#146;s properties in the 
Uruachic mining camp. Under the terms of the agreement, Fresnillo may earn a 
100% interest (subject to a 1% net smelter royalty half of which may be 
purchased for US$500,000) in the La Reforma, Nueva Union, Oteros, Las Bolas, 
Nopalera, La Barranca and Corona properties by making cash payments totaling 
US$3,000,000 over 3 years and by paying all mining rights (property taxes) and 
conducting all assessment work required to keep the properties in good standing.
The Company will keep an undivided 100% interest in its principal property in 
the District, San Timoteo, where work has been focused for the last several 
years.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>During the year, pursuant to a letter of intent 
dated July 14, 2015, Fresnillo advanced $328,254 (4,154,580 Mexican pesos) to 
the Company through two promissory notes in order to initiate negotiations to 
sign the definitive agreement. &nbsp;The promissory notes were unsecured, due on
demand, and bore interest at the Mexican prime rate plus 5% per annum. &nbsp;At 
the signing of the definitive agreement on November 5, 2015, these promissory 
notes were cancelled and the amounts outstanding plus interest were applied to 
the cash payments schedule per the agreement.</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><B>Stock Options</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company has a 10% rolling stock option plan for its directors,
officers, employees and consultants to acquire common shares of the Company at a
price determined by the fair market value of the shares at the date of
grant.&nbsp; The Company&#146;s stock option plan provides for immediate 
vesting, or vesting at the discretion of the Board at the time of the option 
grant and are exercisable for a period of up to 5 years. Stock options granted 
to investor relations&#146; consultants vest over a twelve month period, with 
one quarter of such options vesting in each three month period.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>During the year ended August 31, 2015 all stock option out 
standing were canceled.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Nature and Purpose of Reserves</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The reserves recorded in equity on the Company&#146;s statements 
of financial position is comprised of &#147;Share-based Payments Reserve&#148; 
and is used to recognize the fair value of stock option grants prior to 
exercise, expiry or cancellation and the fair value of other share-based 
consideration paid at the date of payment.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center><B>FOR THE NINE MONTHS ENDED MAY 31, 2016 AND 2015</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt"

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>8.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>LOSS PER SHARE 
</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company calculates the basic and diluted loss per common share
using the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during each 
period and the diluted loss per share assumes that the outstanding vested stock 
options and share purchase warrants had been exercised at the beginning of the 
year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>To compute diluted earnings per share, the average number of 
shares outstanding is adjusted for the number of all potentially dilutive 
shares. &nbsp;As of May 31, 2016, the Company had a total of Nil &nbsp;(August 
31, 2015 &#150; Nil) stock options outstanding. &nbsp;As of May 31, 2016 the 
Company had a total of Nil warrants outstanding (August 31, 2015 - 11,988,888, 
of which 1,155,555 were potentially dilutive). &nbsp;Dilutive options and 
warrants were not included in the Company&#146;s loss per common share 
calculation because the result was anti-dilutive.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt"
align=justify><I>Financial Instrument Risk Exposure and Risk Management</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company is exposed in varying degrees to a variety of 
financial instrument related risks. &nbsp;The Board of Directors approves and 
monitors the risk management process. &nbsp;The overall objective of the Board 
is to set policies that seek to reduce risk as far as possible without unduly 
affecting the Company&#146;s competitiveness and flexibility. The types of risk 
exposure and the way in which such exposure is managed is provided as 
follows:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><I>Credit Risk</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-
size:9pt">Credit risk is the risk that one party to a financial instrument will 
fail to fulfil an obligation and cause the other party to incur a financial 
loss. The Company<FONT style="font-family:Times New Roman">&#146;</FONT>s credit
risk to its financial asset is summarized below: </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

align=center>(An Exploration Stage Company)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt"

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt" 
align=center><B>FOR THE NINE MONTHS ENDED MAY 31, 2016 AND 2015</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt"

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:11pt"

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>10.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>FINANCIAL 
INSTRUMENTS </B>(Continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Liquidity Risk</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Liquidity risk is the risk that the Company will 
encounter difficulties in meeting its financial obligations associated with its 
financial liabilities as they fall due. The Company ensures that there is 
sufficient capital in order to meet short term business requirements, after 
taking into account the Company&#146;s holdings of cash. &nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>As of May 31, 2016, the Company does not have sufficient cash and 
highly liquid investment on hand to meet current liabilities and its expected 
administrative requirements for the coming year. The Company has cash of 
$130,913 (August 31, 2015 - $99,235) and total liabilities of $544,043 (August 
31, 2015 - $653,015). Accounts payable and accrued liabilities and due to 
related parties of $459,289 (August 31, 2015 - $245,087) are due within three 
months. Management has assessed liquidity risk as high.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><I>Market Risk</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The significant market risk exposures to which the Company is 
exposed are foreign exchange risk, interest rate risk, and commodity price risk.
</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><I>Foreign Currency Risk</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company has operations in Canada and Mexico subject to foreign
currency fluctuations. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s operating expenses are incurred 
in Canadian dollars and Mexican pesos, and the fluctuation of the Canadian 
dollar in relation to this other currency will have an impact upon the 
profitability of the Company and may also affect the value of the Company&#146;s
assets and the amount of equity. &nbsp;The Company has not entered into any 
agreements or purchased any instruments to hedge possible currency risks.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>Financial assets and liabilities denominated in Mexican Pesos and 
U.S. dollars were as follows:</P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Based on the above net exposures as at May 31, 
2016, and assuming that all other variables remain constant, a 10% change in the
value of the Mexican peso against the Canadian dollar would result in an 
increase/decrease of approximately $15,073 (August 31, 2015 - $4,400) in loss 
from operations. &nbsp;Based on the above net exposures as at May 31, 2016, and 
assuming that all other variables remain constant, a 10% change in the value of 
the US dollar against the Canadian dollar would result in an increase/decrease 
of approximately $100 (August 31, 2015 - $200) in loss from operations.</P>

&nbsp;&nbsp;FINANCIAL INSTRUMENTS</B> (Continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Interest Rate Risk </I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>As at May 31, 2016, the Company has no significant 
exposure to interest rate risk through its financial instruments.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The Company's operations are in northern Mexico and
are subject to various levels of political, economic and other risks and 
uncertainties unique to Mexico. These risks and uncertainties may include: 
extreme fluctuations in currency exchange rates; high rates of inflation; labor 
unrest; risks of war or civil unrest; expropriation and nationalization; 
renegotiation or nullification of existing concessions, licenses, permits and 
contracts; illegal mining; corruption; restrictions on foreign exchange and 
repatriation; hostage taking; and changing political conditions and currency 
controls. In addition, the Company may have to comply with multiple and 
potentially &nbsp;conflicting regulations in Canada and Mexico, including export
&nbsp;requirements, taxes, tariffs, import duties and other trade barriers, as 
well as health, safety and environmental requirements. &nbsp;Changes, if any, in
mining or investment policies or shifts in political attitude in Mexico may 
adversely affect the Company's operations. Operations may be affected in varying
degrees by government regulations with &nbsp;respect to matters including 
restrictions on production, price controls, export controls, currency controls 
or restrictions, currency &nbsp;remittance, income and other taxes, 
expropriation of property, foreign &nbsp;investment, maintenance of claims, 
environmental legislation, land &nbsp;use, land claims of local people, water 
use and mine safety. Failure &nbsp;to comply strictly with applicable laws, 
regulations and local practices relating to mineral rights applications and 
tenure could result in loss, reduction or expropriation of entitlements or the 
imposition of additional local or foreign parties as joint venture partners with
carried or other interests.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>11.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>CAPITAL DISCLOSURES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company was formed for the purpose of acquiring exploration 
and development stage natural resource properties. &nbsp;The directors determine
the Company&#146;s capital structure and make adjustments to it based on funds 
available to the Company, in order to support the acquisition, exploration and 
development of mineral properties. &nbsp;The directors have not established 
quantitative return on capital criteria for capital management.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt"
align=justify>The Company is dependent upon external financing to fund future 
exploration programs and its administrative costs. The Company will spend 
existing working capital and raise additional amounts as needed. &nbsp;The 
Company will continue to assess new properties and to seek to acquire an 
interest in additional properties if management feels there is sufficient 
geologic or economic potential provided it has adequate financial resources to 
do so.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The directors review the Company&#146;s capital management 
approach on an ongoing basis and believe that this approach, given the relative 
size of the Company, is reasonable. The Company&#146;s objective when managing 
capital is to safeguard the Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going 
concern.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company considers the items included on the statement of 
financial position in equity as capital. &nbsp;The Company manages the capital 
structure and makes adjustments to it in the light of changes in economic 
conditions and the risk characteristics of the underlying assets. &nbsp;In order
to maintain or adjust the capital structure, the Company may issue new shares 
through private placements, sell assets to reduce debt or return capital to 
shareholders. &nbsp;There were no changes to the Company&#146;s approach to 
capital management during the year. &nbsp;Neither the Company nor its 
subsidiaries are subject to externally imposed capital requirements.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>14.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>SUBSEQUENT 
EVENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company announced it granted 3.4 million stock options to its 
directors, officers and consultants exercisable at a price of 8.5 cents for a 
period of five years.</P>

<BODY style="margin-top:0;font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt; 
color:#000000">
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>Management Discussion and 
Analysis</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>For</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>Golden Goliath Resources 
Ltd.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>For the Quarter Ending May
31, 2016</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><B>General</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The following management 
discussion and analysis has been prepared as of July 27, 2016.<B> &nbsp;</B>The 
selected financial information set out below and certain comments which follow 
are based on and derived from the management prepared condensed consolidated 
financial statements of Golden Goliath Resources Ltd. (the &#147;Company&#148; 
or &#147;Golden Goliath&#148;) for the third quarter ending May 31, 2016 and 
should be read in conjunction with them. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Golden Goliath is a Canadian
listed public company with its shares traded on the TSX Venture Exchange under 
the symbol &#147;GNG&#148; as a Tier 2 company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Golden Goliath is a junior 
exploration company with no revenues from mineral producing operations. 
&nbsp;The Company&#146;s properties are all located in the State of Chihuahua, 
Mexico. &nbsp;Activities include acquiring mineral properties and conducting 
exploration programs. &nbsp;The mineral exploration business is risky and most 
exploration projects will not become mines. &nbsp;The Company may offer to a 
major mining company the opportunity to acquire an interest in a property in 
return for funding by the major mining company, of all or part of the 
exploration and development of the property. &nbsp;For the funding of property 
acquisitions and exploration that the Company conducts, the Company does not use
long term debt. &nbsp;Rather, it depends on the issue of shares from the 
treasury to investors. &nbsp;Such stock issues in turn depend on numerous 
factors, important among which are a positive mineral exploration climate, 
positive stock market conditions, a company&#146;s track record and the 
experience of management.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><B>Overall Performance 
</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the quarter ending
May 31, 2016 the Company conducted its 2016 exploration program on its San 
Timoteo property. &nbsp;The 2016 program involved using the Company&#146;s 
Terraspec machine to analyze clay minerals from existing, property wide, drill 
core and other samples including samples from the area of the 500 level San 
Martin adit. The aim of this work was to allow the Company to build a 3D model 
of clay mineralogy to aid in the planning of future drill holes. &nbsp;Because 
different clay minerals form at different temperatures they can be used to 
differentiate different levels in the epithermal system that deposited the 
mineralization. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>When the rising fluids get 
close enough to the surface that the confining pressure of the overlying rock is
no longer sufficient to stop boiling, most of the precious metals are deposited 
and the &#147;bonanza zone&#148; of gold and silver mineralization occurs. 
&nbsp;A specific goal of the 2016 work program was to ensure that the Level 5 
tunnel at San Martin (the lowest old working on the San Timoteo property), is 
above the paleo boiling level indicating greater potential at depth. &nbsp;The 
interpretation of the results confirmed the San Martin tunnel is above this 
level.</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><BR>
The field work portion of the 2016 program was completed during the third fiscal
quarter, but the final report was not finished until the next quarter.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Results of Operation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>For the quarter ended May 
31<FONT style="font-size:12pt">, 2016</FONT>, the Company incurred a 
comprehensive gain of $231,775 compared to comprehensive loss of $153,992 for 
the prior quarter and $135,178 for the quarter ended May 31, 2015. &nbsp;The 
significant differences between these periods include: </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<A NAME="OLE_LINK1"></A><A NAME="OLE_LINK2"></A><P style="margin-top:0px; 
margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; font-size:11pt; 
float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>A gain on the sale of an interest in mineral properties of 
$311,430 in the past quarter compared to nil in prior quarters. &nbsp;The gain 
was a result of the cash payments received from the option of mineral properties
to Fresnillo PLC.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; 
font-size:11pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>Office and general expenses decreased to $21,710 in the past 
quarter compared to $46,362 in the prior quarter as the Company had added costs 
in the second quarter associated with closing the option agreement with 
Fresnillo PLC and commencing activities to conduct a small work program in the 
upcoming season.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; 
font-size:11pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>The Company recorded a gain on foreign currency exchanges of 
$15,153 compared to a loss in the prior quarter of $2,277 and a loss in the 
prior year of $2,820 due to currency exchange rate fluctuations. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; 
font-size:11pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>During the first quarter ended November 30, 2015, the Company 
realized a loss of $75,134 on marketable securities compared to nil in the other
quarters under review due to a loss on the value of marketable securities the 
Company sold.</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>As of <FONT style="font-
size:12pt">May 31, 2016</FONT>, deferred mineral property exploration costs 
totalled $3,229,311 compared to $3,344,949 at August 31, 2015. &nbsp;The
reduction in deferred property costs relate mainly to option payments received 
from Fresnillo and taxes paid by the Company then reimbursed by Fresnillo. 
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

consisting of cash and shares. There were no discontinued operations or 
extraordinary items on the Company&#146;s financial statements during the above 
mentioned periods. &nbsp;The large increase in comprehensive loss in the quarter
ended August 31, 2014 was a result of a property write downs of $2,883,086.</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has financed its
operations almost exclusively through the sale of its common shares to investors
and will be required to continue to do so for the foreseeable future.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company had working 
capital (deficit) of ($245,776) at May 31, 2016 compared to ($146,484) at August
31, 2015. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s cash position at May 31, 2016 was $130,913.
</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Capital Resources</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Other than property taxes 
which are approximately $240,000 per year, the Company does not have any capital
resource commitments. &nbsp;Apart from approximately $40,000 per year, the 
remaining taxes payable are required to be paid by Fresnillo pursuant to the 
option agreement.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; clear:left"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Critical Accounting Estimates</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><I>Exploration and 
Evaluation Assets</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Exploration and evaluation 
expenditures include the costs associated with exploration and evaluation 
activity. Exploration and evaluation expenditures are capitalized as incurred. 
Costs incurred before the Company has obtained the legal rights to explore an 
area are recognized in profit or loss.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Exploration and evaluation 
assets are assessed for impairment if (i) sufficient data exists to determine 
technical feasibility and commercial viability, and (ii) facts and circumstances
suggest that the carrying amount exceeds the recoverable amount.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Once the technical
feasibility and commercial viability of the extraction of mineral resources in 
an area of interest are demonstrable, which management has determined to be 
indicated by a feasibility study, exploration and evaluation assets attributable
to that area of interest are first tested for impairment and then reclassified 
to mining property and development assets.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Recoverability of the 
carrying amount of any exploration and evaluation assets is dependent on 
successful development and commercial exploitation, or alternatively, sale of 
the respective areas of interest.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>It is management&#146;s 
judgment that none of the Company&#146;s exploration and evaluation assets have 
reached the development stage and as a result are all considered to be 
exploration and evaluation assets. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Although the Company has 
taken steps to verify title to mineral properties in which it has an interest, 
in accordance with industry standards for the current stage of exploration of 
such properties, these procedures do not guarantee the Company&#146;s title. 
Property may be subject to unregistered prior agreements and non-compliance with
regulatory requirements. The Company is not aware of any disputed claims of 
title.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

Instruments</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has not entered 
into any specialized financial agreements to minimize its investment risk, 
currency risk or commodity risk. &nbsp;As of the date hereof, the Company&#146;s
investment in resource properties has full exposure to commodity risk, both 
upside and downside. &nbsp;As the metal prices move so too does the underlying 
value of the Company&#146;s metal projects.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Disclosure Controls and 
Procedures</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Disclosure controls and 
procedures (&#147;DC&amp;P&#148;) are intended to provide reasonable assurance 
that information required to be disclosed is recorded, processed, summarized and
reported within the time periods specified by securities regulations and that 
information required to be disclosed is accumulated and communicated to 
management. &nbsp;Internal controls over financial reporting (&#147;ICFR&#148;) 
are intended to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of 
financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external 
purpose in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting
principles.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>TSX Venture listed companies
are not required to provide representations in the annual filings relating to 
the establishment and maintenance of DC&amp;P and ICFR, as defined in 
Multinational Instrument 52-109. &nbsp;In particular, the CEO and CFO certifying
officers do not make any representations relating to the establishment and 
maintenance of (a) controls and other procedures designed to provide reasonable 
assurance that information required to be disclosed by the issuer in its annual 
filings, interim filings or other reports filed or submitted under securities 
legislation is recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time 
periods specified in securities legislation, and (b) a process to provide 
reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the 
preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with the
issuer&#146;s GAAP. &nbsp;The issuer&#146;s certifying officers are responsible 
for ensuring that processes are in place to provide them with sufficient 
knowledge to support the representations they are making in their certificates 
regarding the absence of misrepresentations and fair disclosure of financial 
information. &nbsp;Investors should be aware that inherent limitation on the 
ability of certifying officers of a venture issuer to design and implement on a 
cost effective basis DC&amp;P and ICFR as defined in Multinational Instrument 
52-109 may result in additional risks to the quality, reliability, transparency 
and timeliness of interim and annual filings and other reports provided under 
securities legislation. &nbsp;</P>
